Mubashara Fahisha: Nullification of Wudu
Discusses whether direct skin-to-skin contact between spouses with arousal nullifies wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on mubashara fahisha and explain the reasoning based on the hadith and istihsan.

Core Idea
Mubashara fahisha with arousal nullifies wudu — the apparent cause replaces the hidden impurity.

This lesson explores whether direct physical contact between spouses with arousal nullifies wudu. The Hanafi school has internal differences, but the relied-upon view is that it does, based on a hadith and the principle of istihsan. We will analyze the reasoning of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and the objection of Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on mubashara fahisha
Identify the act, its ruling (nullifier of wudu), and the conditions that trigger it (arousal and skin-to-skin contact). Note the difference between the relied-upon view and the requirement of direct genital contact.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the relied-upon view is from the two shaykhs.
2
Identify the opposing view of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad holds that mubashara fahisha does not nullify wudu by qiyas. Understand his reasoning: the cause (contact) should not replace the effect (impurity) when the effect is easily ascertainable.
Muhammad's view is based on original qiyas but is outweighed by hadith and istihsan.
3
Analyze the proof for the relied-upon view
Examine the hadith of Abu al-Yusur where the Prophet ordered wudu after everything except intercourse. Also understand the istihsan argument: the apparent cause (contact) stands in for the hidden impurity because it is rarely absent in such situations.
The hadith is not mutawatir but is accepted as a sound basis for the ruling.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its scope
The correct view according to later authorities (e.g., al-Tuhfah) is that of the two shaykhs. This extends to women and same-sex contact. Understand the principle that rulings for men generally apply to women unless specified.
The passage also clarifies that direct contact between men or with a boy necessitates wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ومباشرة فاحشة) يعني أن من النواقض الحكمية المباشرة الفاحشة امرأته متجردين ولاقى فرجها مع انتشار الآلة ولم ير بللاً، ولم يشترط بعضم ملاقاة الفرج والظاهر الأول كذا ذكر الزيلعي، لكن المنقول في البدائع أن في ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لم يشترط مماستهما وشرط ذلك في النوادر وذكره الكرخي أيضاً ا هـ. ظاهر الرواية عدم الاشتراط وكذا ذكر في الينابيع وقال : وروى الحسن أنه يشترط وهو فقول من قال الظاهر الاشتراط أراد من جهة الدراية لا الرواية، وصحح الاسبيجابي اشتراطه بعد أن ذكر أن ظاهر الرواية عدمه والقياس أن لا يكون حدثاً وهو قول محمد، لأن السبب إنما يقام مقام المسبب في موضع لا يمكن الوقوف على المسبب من غير حرج والوقوف على المسبب هنا ممكن بلا حرج لأن الحال حال يقظة فلا حاجة إلى الإقامة. وجه وهو قولهما ما روي أن أبا اليسر بائع العسل سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال : أني أصبت من امرأتي كل شيء إلا الجماع فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: توضأ وصل ركعتين». كذا البدائع والله أعلم بصحة هذا الحديث ولأنه يندر عدم مذي مع هذه الحالة والغالب كالمتحقق في مقام وجوب الاحتياط والأصل أن السبب الظاهر يقوم مقام الأمر الباطن وذلك بطريق قيام هذه المباشرة مقام خروج النجس كذا في المصفى. وفي الحقائق شرح المنظومة معزياً إلى فتاوى العتابي روي عن أصحابنا أنه لا ينقض ما لم يظهر شيء هو الصحيح ولا يعتمد على هذا التصحيح فقد صرح في التحفة كما نقله شارح المنية أن الصحيح قولهما وهو المذكور في المتون. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى القنية وكذا المباشرة بين الرجل والغلام، وكذا بين الرجلين توجب الوضوء عليهما. وفي شرح منية المصلي معزياً إليها أيضاً أن الوضوء يجب على المرأة من المباشرة أيضاً قال : ولم أقف عليه إلا في القنية وفيه تأمل فإنهم لم يذكروا في مباشرة الرجل للمرأة على وقولهما إلا على الرجل ا هـ . وقد يقال لا حاجة إلى التنصيص على الحكم في المرأة فإن من المعلوم أن كل حكم ثبت للرجال ثبت للنساء لأنهن شقائق الرجال إلا ما نص عليه قال في المستصفى الأصل في النساء أن لا يذكرن لأن مبني حالهن على الستر ولهذا لم يذكرن في القرآن حتى شكون فنزل قوله تعالى إن المسلمين والمسلمات ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٣٥] إلا إذا كان الحكم مخصوصاً بهن كمسألة الصغيرة الآتية في الغسل ا ولأنه قد وقع في كثير من عبارات علمائنا أن المباشرة الفاحشة تنقض الوضوء ولم يقيدوا بوضوء الرجل فكان وضوءها داخلاً فيه كما لا يخفى.
His statement: “And direct physical contact (mubashara fahisha)” means that among the hukmi (non-explicit) nullifiers is direct physical contact with one’s wife when both are unclothed, and his genitals touch hers with arousal of the organ, and he sees no fluid. Some did not require direct contact of the genitals; the apparent first is as mentioned by al-Zayla‘i. However, it is reported in al-Bada’i that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, they did not require their direct touching, but it was required in the Nawadir, and al-Karkhi also mentioned it. So the apparent narration is non-requirement, and likewise mentioned in al-Yanabi‘. He said: Al-Hasan narrated that it is required, and it is a saying. Whoever said the apparent is requirement meant from the perspective of diraya, not riwaya. Al-Isbijabi held the requirement as sahih after mentioning that the apparent narration is non-requirement. And the qiyas is that it should not be a hadath, and that is the saying of Muhammad, because the cause is only placed in the position of the effect in a place where ascertaining the effect is not possible without difficulty, while ascertaining the effect here is possible without difficulty because the situation is wakefulness, so there is no need for substitution. The justification (for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is what was reported that Abu al-Yusur, a honey seller, asked the Messenger of Allah and said: “I have done everything with my wife except intercourse.” The Messenger of Allah said: “Perform wudu and pray two rak‘ahs.” (Al-Bada’i; and Allah knows best the authenticity of this hadith.) And because it is rare that there is no pre-ejaculatory fluid in this situation, and the predominant is like the certain in the context of obligatory precaution. And the principle is that the apparent cause takes the place of the hidden matter, and that is by way of this direct contact taking the place of the exit of impurity, as in al-Musaffa. In al-Haqa’iq Sharh al-Manzumah, attributed to Fatawa al-‘Itabi: It is narrated from our companions that it does not nullify unless something appears; that is the correct view. But do not rely on this tashih, for it is clear in al-Tuhfah, as quoted by the commentator of al-Munyah, that the correct view is that of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), which is mentioned in the matn. In Fath al-Qadir, attributed to al-Qunyah: Likewise, direct contact between a man and a boy, and between two men, necessitates wudu for both. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, attributed to it also: Wudu is obligatory for a woman from direct contact as well. He said: I have not found it except in al-Qunyah, and it requires consideration, for they did not mention regarding direct contact of a man with a woman except on the man. It may be said: There is no need to specify the ruling for women, for it is known that every ruling established for men is established for women, because they are halves of men, except where specified. Al-Mustasfa said: The principle is that women are not mentioned because their situation is based on concealment; therefore they were not mentioned in the Qur’an until they complained, then the verse “Indeed, the Muslim men and Muslim women” (33:35) was revealed, unless the ruling is specific to them, like the issue of the young girl in ghusl. And because it has occurred in many statements of our scholars that direct physical contact nullifies wudu, and they did not restrict it to a man’s wudu, so her wudu is included, as is evident.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of mubashara fahisha (direct physical contact) between spouses and its effect on wudu. The author explains that this is one of the hukmi (non-explicit) nullifiers of wudu. The basic scenario: a man and his wife are unclothed, their genitals touch with arousal, but no emission occurs. The key point of disagreement within the Hanafi school is whether actual direct contact of the genitals (mulasat al-farj) is required. The text states that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, direct contact of the genitals is not required; mere skin-to-skin contact with arousal suffices. However, in the Nawadir (rare narrations), it is required, and al-Karkhi also mentioned that. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds, based on qiyas, that such contact should not be a nullifier at all, because the cause (contact) only substitutes for the effect (exit of impurity) when the effect cannot be easily ascertained; but here, the effect (e.g., pre-ejaculate) can be checked without difficulty. The justification for the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is a hadith where the Prophet ordered someone who had done everything except intercourse to perform wudu. This indicates that wudu becomes obligatory due to such contact, based on the principle that the apparent cause (contact) stands in for the hidden matter (impurity) due to rarity of its absence. The author notes that the correct view (sahih) according to later scholars like the author of al-Tuhfah is the view of the two shaykhs (non-requirement of direct genital contact). The passage also extends the ruling to other cases: contact between a man and a boy, and between two men, also necessitates wudu for both. For women, the text mentions that wudu is obligatory on the woman as well, citing al-Qunyah, though some scholars questioned this. However, the general principle is that rulings for men apply to women unless specified otherwise.

Key Terms
المباشرة الفاحشة (al-mubashara al-fahisha): Direct physical contact between a man and a woman (or between two males) that is sexually arousing, typically with skin-to-skin contact. It is considered a hukmi nullifier of wudu in the Hanafi school.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent and most widespread narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, transmitted through their six major books. It is the primary source of authority within the Hanafi school.
الانتشار (al-intishar): Arousal of the male organ (erection). In the context of mubashara fahisha, it is a condition for the nullification of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position on mubashara fahisha, which of the following is required for wudu to be nullified?
A) Emission of fluid
B) Direct genital contact
C) Arousal and skin-to-skin contact
D) Intention to nullify wudu

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that mubashara fahisha with arousal nullifies wudu for both parties, based on a prophetic hadith and the principle of istihsan.

Intimate Contact Without Discharge: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wudu Nullification
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on nullification of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi positions on whether intimate contact without discharge nullifies wudu, identify the evidence for each, and explain why the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Intimate contact without discharge nullifies wudu according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but not according to Imam Muhammad.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines an intra-Hanafi dispute. While the authoritative transmission (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf holds that even intimate contact without any discharge invalidates wudu, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees based on qiyas. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh proofs within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
Define 'mubasharah fahishah' (intimate direct contact without intercourse) and state the issue: does it nullify wudu when no discharge occurs?
The act occurs between spouses while naked, with arousal.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that wudu is nullified even without skin-to-skin contact, based on the hadith of Abu al-Yusr.
Zahir al-riwayah supports non-stipulation of skin contact.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
He holds it does not nullify because the cause (discharge) can be verified without hardship, so no need to substitute the act for the effect.
This is based on qiyas: the effect (discharge) is ascertainable during wakefulness.
4
State the position from al-Nawadir (al-Hasan ibn Ziyad)
Al-Hasan requires actual skin contact for nullification, but this view is from rare transmissions and is not relied upon.
Some later scholars like al-Karkhi mention this, but it is not part of zahir al-riwayah.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and the tarjih
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as affirmed by al-Marghinani and other later authorities.
The dominant practice (fatwa) follows the view of the two imams.

والأصل أن السبب الظاهر يقوم مقام الأمر الباطن وذلك بطريق قيام هذه المباشرة مقام خروج النجس كذا في المصفى. وفي الحقائق شرح المنظومة معزياً إلى فتاوى العتابي روي عن أصحابنا أنه لا ينقض ما لم يظهر شيء هو الصحيح ولا يعتمد على هذا التصحيح فقد صرح في التحفة كما نقله شارح المنية أن الصحيح قولهما وهو المذكور في المتون. وفي فتح القدير معزياً إلى القنية وكذا المباشرة بين الرجل والغلام، وكذا بين الرجلين توجب الوضوء عليهما. وفي شرح منية المصلي معزياً إليها أيضاً أن الوضوء يجب على المرأة من المباشرة أيضاً قال : ولم أقف عليه إلا في القنية وفيه تأمل فإنهم لم يذكروا في مباشرة الرجل للمرأة على وقولهما إلا على علمائنا أن المباشرة الفاحشة تنقض الوضوء ولم يقيدوا بوضوء الرجل فكان وضوءها داخلاً فيه كما لا يخفى.
The istihsan: it is to directly engage. So it is known that the apparent [view] in his saying (and engaging in obscene contact) means that among the legal nullifiers is engaging in obscene contact with his wife while both are naked, and his private part contacts hers with arousal, and he sees no wetness. And some did not stipulate contact of the private parts, and the apparent is the first, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. However, what is transmitted in al-Bada'i' is that in the zahir al-riwayah from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, they did not stipulate mutual contact, and that was stipulated in al-Nawadir, and al-Karkhi also mentioned it. The zahir al-riwayah is non-stipulation, and likewise mentioned in al-Yanabi', and he said: al-Hasan narrated that it is stipulated, and it is a statement of one who said the apparent is stipulation, meaning by way of insight, not narration. Al-Asbijabi corrected its stipulation after mentioning that the zahir al-riwayah is without it, and the qiyas is that it is not an event, and that is the view of Muhammad, because a cause is only made to stand in place of the effect in a situation where it is impossible to ascertain the effect without hardship, and ascertaining the effect here is possible without hardship because the situation is one of wakefulness, so there is no need for substitution. And the proof for their view is what was narrated that Abu al-Yusr, the honey seller, asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and said: 'I have done everything with my wife except intercourse.' The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Perform wudu and pray two rak'ahs.' So [it is] in al-Bada'i', and Allah knows best about the authenticity of this hadith. And because it is rare that there is no madhy in this situation, and the prevalent is like the certain in the position of necessity of precaution, and the principle is that the apparent cause stands in place of the hidden matter, and that is by way of this direct contact standing in place of the exit of impurity, as in al-Musaffa. And in al-Haqa'iq Sharh al-Manzumah, attributed to Fatawa al-'Attabi, it is narrated from our companions that it does not nullify unless something appears, and that is the correct [view], but this correction is not relied upon, for it is explicitly stated in al-Tuhfah, as quoted by the commentator of al-Munyah, that the correct view is that of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and it is what is mentioned in the texts. And in Fath al-Qadir, attributed to al-Qunyah, likewise direct contact between a man and a boy, and likewise between two men, obligates wudu upon both. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, attributed to it as well, that wudu is obligatory upon a woman from [such] direct contact also. He said: I have not come across it except in al-Qunyah, and there is consideration in it, for they did not mention in the case of a man's direct contact with a woman, based on their view, except upon the man. It may be said: there is no need to specify the ruling for women, for it is known that every ruling established for men is established for women because they are the counterparts of men, except where explicitly stated otherwise. He said in al-Mustasfa: the principle concerning women is that they are not mentioned because their state is based on concealment, and for this reason they were not mentioned in the Qur'an until they complained, so Allah revealed {Indeed, the Muslim men and Muslim women} [al-Ahzab:35] unless the ruling is specific to them, like the issue of the minor girl coming in ghusl. And because it occurs in many expressions of our scholars that obscene direct contact nullifies wudu, and they did not restrict it to a man's wudu, so her wudu is included in it, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether intimate direct contact (mubasharah fahishah) between a man and his wife, without any discharge, nullifies wudu. The author first presents the istihsan view, noting that in the zahir al-riwayah (the authoritative transmission from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) there is no requirement of actual skin-to-skin contact, while in the nawadir (rare narrations) from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, contact is stipulated. Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani holds that it does not nullify at all, based on qiyas: since the cause (discharge) is directly ascertainable, there is no need to substitute it with the act of contact. The proof for the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the hadith of Abu al-Yusr, where the Prophet ordered wudu after everything except intercourse, indicating that contact without discharge still necessitates wudu. The author also argues that since it is rare to have no madhy (pre-ejaculatory fluid) in such situations, the dominant case is treated as certain for precaution. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, that such contact does nullify wudu. The passage also extends the ruling to women, men and boys, and two men, and clarifies that women are included in the general rulings unless specified otherwise.

Key Terms
مباشرة فاحشة (mubāsharah fāḥishah): Intimate direct contact between a man and a woman without a barrier, typically involving the genitals, without actual intercourse.
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The transmitted reports from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the core Hanafi doctrine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both parties must be naked and the private parts touch
D) The male must see discharge

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that intimate contact with arousal nullifies wudu, regardless of discharge or skin-to-skin contact, based on the hadith of Abu al-Yusr and the prevalence of madhy.

Does Touching the Penis Nullify Wudu? The Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on nullification of wudu by touching genitals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mass al-dhakar and explain the Shafi'i counterargument and the Hanafi response using dalil.

Core Idea
Touching the penis does not nullify wudu in the Hanafi school, contrary to Shafi'i.

A common question among Muslims is whether touching one's genitals breaks wudu. The four schools differ. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position, its evidence, and the Shafi'i objection. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the ruling and introduces the key hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the text: wudu is not nullified by touching the penis, anus, or vagina, regardless of the part of the hand used.
The text says 'wudu is not nullified by touching the penis, and likewise the anus and vagina absolutely'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that touching these parts with the inner palm nullifies wudu.
The text says 'contrary to al-Shafi'i; for according to him, touching any one of the three nullifies wudu if it is with the inner part of the fingers.'
3
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan: 'When one of you touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' This is a hasan hadith narrated by Malik, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah.
The text cites this hadith as the Shafi'i evidence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is a hadith narrated by the authors of the Sunan except Ibn Majah. This hadith indicates that the Prophet did not renew wudu after touching, or that touching does not necessitate wudu. The text is cut off but implies this.
The Hanafis interpret the hadith of Busrah as recommending rather than obligating wudu.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis do not require wudu after touching genitals; Shafi'is do. A Shafi'i who prays without renewing wudu after touching would consider his prayer invalid, while a Hanafi's prayer remains valid.
This affects prayer validity and daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ومس ذكر بالرفع عطف على المنفي أي لا ينقض الوضوء مس الذكر وكذا مس الدبر والفرج مطلقاً خلافاً للشافعي فإن المس لواحد من الثلاثة ناقض للوضوء إذا كان بباطن الأصابع. واستدل النووي له في شرح المهذب بما روت بسرة بنت صفوان أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «إذا مس أحدكم ذكره فليتوضأ» (۱) وهو حديث حسن رواه مالك في الموطأ وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه بأسانيد صحيحة ولنا ما رواه الجماعة أصحاب السنن إلا ابن ماجه
His saying (and touching the penis, in the nominative case, is connected to the negated [items]) meaning: wudu is not nullified by touching the penis, and likewise touching the anus and the vagina absolutely, contrary to al-Shafi'i. For according to him, touching any one of the three nullifies wudu if it is with the inner part of the fingers. Al-Nawawi argued for him in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab with what Busrah bint Safwan narrated: that the Prophet ﷺ said 'When one of you touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' It is a good hadith, narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta', Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah with authentic chains. And we [Hanafis] have [the hadith] narrated by the group of the authors of the Sunan except Ibn Majah...
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether touching the penis (or anus/vagina) nullifies wudu. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that it does NOT nullify wudu, contrary to the Shafi'i school. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan, which is considered hasan and narrated by multiple sources. The Hanafi proof (which is cut off in the text) is a hadith narrated by the majority of Sunan authors except Ibn Majah, which indicates that the Prophet himself touched his penis or did not order wudu after touching. The Hanafis interpret the hadith of Busrah as recommendatory (nadb) rather than obligatory (wujub), based on other evidence. The passage also mentions that the ruling applies to touching the anus and vagina as well.

Key Terms
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the male genital organ with the hand.
باطن الأصابع (bāṭin al-aṣābiʿ): The inner part of the fingers; the palm side of the hand used in touching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, touching the genitals does not nullify wudu, though it is recommended to renew wudu to differ with Shafi'i.

Why a Worm from a Wound Does Not Nullify Wudu
Explaining why a worm from a wound does not nullify wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a worm exiting from a wound versus from the private parts and explain the three Hanafi rational distinctions.

Core Idea
A worm from a wound does not nullify wudu because it is generated from flesh, not impurity.

The Hanafi school teaches that the nullification of wudu depends not just on what exits, but from where it exits and how it is generated. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents three sharp legal distinctions that separate the ruling for a worm from a wound from a worm from the private parts. Understanding these distinctions sharpens your ability to apply the school's principles to unusual cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a worm exiting from a wound. The ruling: does not nullify wudu (stated in the matn).
This is the starting point: the text clearly states the ruling.
2
Locate the general principle
Exits from the two passages (anus and genitals) nullify wudu. The worm from a wound is an exception, so the text explains why.
Contrast between the ruling for private parts and wound.
3
Analyse the three distinctions (faces)
First: trace moisture (bulla) is minor impurity; from passage nullifies, from wound does not. Second: the worm itself is pure; pure substance from passage nullifies (like wind), from wound does not. Third: worm from wound is generated from flesh (lahm), like a piece of flesh separating; worm from passage generated from impurity.
These three faces are given as rational proofs (talil) for the ruling.
4
Apply qiyas
The asl (original case) is worm from private parts nullifying; illa (effective cause) is generation from impurity; far' (new case) is worm from wound generated from flesh; hence no nullification.
The qiyas shows the legal reasoning behind the ruling.
5
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Sadr al-Shari'ah held that worm from urethra does not nullify, and there is difference about female genitals. The commentator reconciles by stating no difference between anus, female genitals, and penis.
The commentator upholds the majority view that all private part exits nullify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (لا خروج دودة من جرح بالرفع عطف على خروج نجس أي لا ينقض الوضوء خروج دودة من جرح قيد به لأن الدودة الخارجة من أحد السبيلين تنقض الوضوء، والفرق بينهما من ثلاثة أوجه الأول أن الدودة لا تخلو عن قليل بلة تكون معها وتستصحبها وتلك البلة قليل نجاسة، وقليل النجاسة إذا خرجت من أحد السبيلين انتقض الوضوء ومن غيرهما غير ناقضة. الثاني أن الدودة حيوان وهو طاهر في الأصل والشيء الطاهر إذا خرج من السبيلين نقض الوضوء كالريح بخلاف غير السبيلين كالدمع والعرق. الثالث أن الدودة في الجرح متولدة من اللحم فصار كما لو انفصل قطعة من اللحم فإنه لا ينقض، وأما في السبيلين تتولد من النجاسة فتكون في الخروج كالنجاسة الخارجة من أحدهما والخارج من السبيلين، ناقض وقد قدمنا أنه لا فرق بين الدودة الخارجة من الدبر والقبل والذكر به يندمع ما ذكره صدر الشريعة أن الدودة من الاحليل لا تنقض وأن الدودة من القبل فيها اختلاف المشايخ . وفي شرح مسكين معزياً إلى الذخيرة : إن كان الماء يسيل من الجرح ينقض الوضوء، ولا ينافيه ما في السراج الوهاج أنه لو دخل الماء في الجرح ثم خرج لا ينقض كما لا يخفى بأدنى تأمل .
His saying: (not exiting of a worm from a wound) with the nominative case as an adjunct to the negated item, meaning: the exiting of a worm from a wound does not nullify wudu. It is restricted because the worm exiting from one of the two passages (anus or penis) nullifies wudu. The difference between the two is from three aspects: First, the worm is not free from a slight moisture that accompanies it, and that moisture is a small impurity. A small impurity, if it exits from one of the two passages, wudu is nullified; from other than them, it is not nullifying. Second, the worm is an animal and it is originally pure. A pure thing, if it exits from the two passages, nullifies wudu, like wind, unlike other than the two passages, like tears and sweat. Third, the worm in the wound is generated from flesh, so it becomes as if a piece of flesh separated; it does not nullify. As for the two passages, it is generated from impurity, so in exiting it is like impurity exiting from one of them, and that exiting from the two passages is nullifying. We have already mentioned that there is no difference between a worm exiting from the anus, the female genitals, and the penis, and by this is obviated what Sadr al-Shari'ah mentioned: that a worm from the urethra does not nullify, and that regarding a worm from the female genitals there is difference among the mashayikh. In Sharh Miskin, attributed to al-Dhakhirah: If water flows from the wound, it nullifies wudu. And it does not contradict what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that if water enters the wound then exits, it does not nullify, as is not hidden with minimal reflection.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof explaining that the exit of a worm from a wound does not nullify wudu, unlike if it exits from the private parts (anus, penis, or female genitals). The commentator presents three rational distinctions (faces) validated by Hanafi methodology. First, a worm from a wound always carries some moisture; if that moisture were from a private part it would be considered a small amount of impurity (najasa) that nullifies wudu, but since it comes from elsewhere it does not. Second, the worm itself is pure. A pure substance exiting from the private parts nullifies wudu (like wind), but from other body parts it does not (like tears or sweat). Third, the worm in a wound is generated from the body's own flesh (lahm), so it is treated like a detached piece of flesh—not nullifying. In contrast, a worm from the private parts is generated from impurity (najasa), so it is like actual impurity. The text then notes that Sadr al-Shari'ah's view about the urethra is reconciled, and mentions a ruling from al-Dhakhirah: if water from the wound flows out, it does nullify wudu, but this does not contradict the ruling about water entering then exiting.

Key Terms
النقض (al-naqḍ): Nullification of wudu; an event that breaks the state of ritual purity.
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages: anus and penis (or urethra); also includes female genitals.
البلة (al-bullā): Moisture; here it means the trace moisture accompanying the worm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a worm from a wound not nullify wudu according to the three faces?
A) Because it is too small.
B) Because it is generated from flesh, not impurity.
C) Because it is pure and pure things never nullify.
D) Because it is from outside the body.

Key Takeaway
A worm from a wound does not nullify wudu because it is generated from the body's flesh, not from impurity in the private parts.

Touching the Penis Does Not Nullify Wudu
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the genitals and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Touching the penis is like touching any other limb—it does not break wudu.

You may have heard that touching private parts nullifies wudu, but the Hanafi school holds otherwise. In this lesson, we examine the primary hadith evidence and the arguments that give the Hanafi position its strength, drawing from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that touching the penis, anus, or female genitals does not nullify wudu. This is the default ruling in Hanafi fiqh.
The matn says 'wa mass dhakar' (and touching the penis) as a conjunct to the negated item, i.e., it is added to the list of things that do not nullify.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Look at the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan that commands wudu after touching the penis. This is the opposing school's primary evidence.
The hadith is hasan by al-Tirmidhi and narrated by Malik, Abu Dawud, etc.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Study the hadith of Talq ibn Ali: 'Is it anything but a piece of flesh of yours?' This provides a rationale that touching has no special effect.
The Hanafis argue this hadith is more authentic and based on a clear rationale (ta'lil) that cannot be abrogated.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand why Talq's hadith is preferred: stronger transmission (men narrators), Busrah's hadith weakened by Yahya ibn Ma'in and others, and the claim of abrogation refuted.
The commentator also refutes al-Nawawi's attempt to interpret Talq's hadith as referring to touching over a barrier.
5
Determine the practical consequence
A Hanafi may pray after touching his genitals without renewing wudu; a Shafi'i must renew if touched with inner palm.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf—the practical difference between the schools.

Source Text

قوله (ومس ذكر بالرفع عطف على المنفي أي لا ينقض الوضوء مس الذكر وكذا مس الدبر والفرج مطلقاً خلافاً للشافعي فإن المس لواحد من الثلاثة ناقض للوضوء إذا كان بباطن الأصابع. واستدل النووي له في شرح المهذب بما روت بسرة بنت صفوان أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «إذا مس أحدكم ذكره فليتوضأ» (۱) وهو حديث حسن رواه مالك في الموطأ وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه بأسانيد صحيحة ولنا ما رواه الجماعة أصحاب السنن إلا ابن ماجه عن ملازم بن عمرو عن عبد الله بن بدر عن قيس بن طلق بن علي عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه سئل عن الرجل يمس ذكره في الصلاة فقال : هل هو إلا بضعة منك. وقد رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه قال الترمذي هذا الحديث أحسن شيء يروى في هذا الباب وأصح، ورواه الطحاوي أيضاً وقال : هذا حديث مستقيم الإسناد غير مضطرب في إسناده ومتنه. فهذا حديث صحيح معارض حديث بسرة بنت صفوان ويرجح حديث طلق على حديث بسرة بأن حديث الرجال أقوى لأنهم أحفظ للعلم وأضبط ولهذا جعلت شهادة امرأتين بشهادة رجل وقد اسند الطحاوي إلى ابن المديني أنه قال : حديث ملازم ابن عمرو أحسن من حديث بسرة. وعن عمرو بن علي الفلاس أنه قال : حديث طلق عندنا أثبت من حديث بسرة بنت صفوان، وقول النووي في شرح المهذب أن حديث طلق اتفق على ضعفه لا يخفى ما فيه إذ قد علمت ما قاله الترمذي وغيره أن حديث بسرة ضعفه جماعة حتى قال يحيى بن معين : ثلاثة أحاديث لم تصح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم منها حديث مس الذكر. وقول النووي أيضاً ترجيحاً لحديث بسرة بأن حديث طلق منسوخ لأن قدومه على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان في السنة الأولى من الهجرة ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يبني مسجده وراوي حديث بسرة أبو هريرة، وإنما قدم أبو هريرة على النبي سنة سبع من الهجرة فغير لازم لأن ورود طلق إذ ذاك ثم رجوعه لا ذلك ينفي عوده بعد قد رووا عنه حديثاً ضعيفاً من مس ذكره فليتوضأ» وقالوا : سمع من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الناسخ والمنسوخ، ولأن حديث طلق غير قابل للنسخ لأنه صدر على سبيل التعليل فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ذكر أن الذكر قطعة لحم فلا تأثير لمسه في الانتقاض، وهذا المعنى لا يقبل النسخ، كذا في معراج الدراية. وقول النووي أيضاً إن حديث طلق محمول على المس فوق حائل لأنه قال سألته عن مس الذكر في الصلاة والظاهر أن الإنسان لا ذكره في الصلاة بلا حائل مردود بأن تعليله بقوله هل هو إلا بضعة منك»(۱) يأبى الحمل. والبضعة بفتح الموحدة القطعة من اللحم، وفي شرح الآثار للطحاوي لا نعمل أحداً من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء من مس الذكر إلا ابن عمر وقد خالفه في ذلك أكثرهم، وأسند عن ابن عيينة أنه عد جماعة لم يكونوا يعرفون الحديث يعني حديث بسرة ومن رأيناه يحدث تحامل يسير . قال وخرج ببطن الكف غيره كرؤوس الأصابع وما بينها وحرفها وحرف الراحة، واختص الحكم بباطن الكف وهو الراحة مع بطون الأصابع لأن التلذذ إنما يكون به اهـ.
His saying: (And touching the penis) with nominative as a conjunct to the negated item, i.e., touching the penis does not nullify wudu, and likewise touching the anus and the female genitals absolutely, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for whom touching any of the three nullifies wudu if it is with the inner part of the fingers. Al-Nawawi argued for him in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab with what was narrated by Busrah bint Safwan that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'If any of you touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' This is a hasan hadith narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta', Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah with authentic chains. Our proof is what was narrated by the group of authors of the Sunan except Ibn Majah, from Mulazim ibn Amr from Abdullah ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali from his father from the Prophet (SAW): He was asked about a man touching his penis in prayer, and he said: 'Is it anything but a piece of flesh of yours?' Ibn Hibban narrated it in his Sahih, al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is the best thing narrated on this chapter and the most authentic. Al-Tahawi narrated it and said: This hadith is straightforward in its chain, not disordered in its chain or text. So this hadith is sahih, contradicting the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan, and the hadith of Talq is preferred over the hadith of Busrah because the hadith of men is stronger, as they are more retentive of knowledge and more accurate; for this reason the testimony of two women is made equal to the testimony of one man. Al-Tahawi ascribed to Ibn al-Madini that he said: The hadith of Mulazim ibn Amr is better than the hadith of Busrah. Amr ibn Ali al-Fallas said: The hadith of Talq is more firmly established with us than the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan. Al-Nawawi's statement in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that the hadith of Talq is agreed upon as weak is not hidden in what we have already known: what al-Tirmidhi and others said that the hadith of Busrah was declared weak by a group, even Yahya ibn Ma'in said: Three hadiths are not authentic from the Messenger of Allah, among them the hadith of touching the penis. Al-Nawawi's further argument to prefer Busrah's hadith that Talq's hadith is abrogated because his arrival to the Prophet was in the first year of Hijrah while the Prophet was building his mosque, while the narrator of Busrah's hadith is Abu Hurayrah who only came in the seventh year of Hijrah, is not necessary because Talq's presence at that time and then his return does not negate his return later; they narrated from him a weak hadith 'who touches his penis let him perform wudu' and they said he heard from the Prophet the abrogating and abrogated. Also, Talq's hadith is not subject to abrogation because it was stated as a rationale: he (SAW) mentioned that the penis is a piece of flesh, so touching it has no effect on nullification, and this meaning is not subject to abrogation. So it is in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. Al-Nawawi's further statement that Talq's hadith is interpreted as touching over a barrier because he said 'I asked him about touching the penis in prayer' and apparently a person does not touch his penis in prayer without a barrier is refuted by his rationalization: 'Is it anything but a piece of flesh of yours?' which precludes such interpretation. Al-bad'ah is a piece of flesh (with fatha on the ba). In Sharh al-Athar of al-Tahawi: We do not know any Companion who gave a fatwa of wudu from touching the penis except Ibn Umar, and most of them differed with him. He also ascribed from Ibn Uyaynah that he counted a group who did not know the hadith—meaning the hadith of Busrah—and those we see narrating it, there is slight bias. He said: And what is excluded from the palm of the hand is other than it, like the tips of the fingers, between them, their edge, and the edge of the palm. The ruling is specific to the inner palm, which is the palm with the inner parts of the fingers, because pleasure is only from it. End.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether touching the penis (or anus/female genitals) nullifies wudu. The author states the Hanafi position (from the matn) that it does not nullify. He then presents the Shafi'i position (as argued by al-Nawawi) that it does nullify if touched with the inner palm/fingers, citing the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan. The Hanafi response is thorough: they present the hadith of Talq ibn Ali (narrated by his son Qays) that the Prophet said 'Is it anything but a piece of flesh of yours?' This hadith is declared authentic by al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, and al-Tahawi. The commentator then provides detailed arguments for preferring Talq's hadith: men's narrations are stronger than women's; the hadith of Busrah was weakened by many scholars including Yahya ibn Ma'in; the claim of abrogation is rebutted because Talq's hadith is based on a rationale (ta'lil) that cannot be abrogated; and the attempt to interpret Talq's hadith as referring to touching over a barrier is refuted by the clear wording 'piece of flesh'. The passage ends by noting that most Companions did not hold the view of wudu from touching, except Ibn Umar. The ruling is specific to inner palm; other parts do not nullify even according to Shafi'i.

Key Terms
بضعة (biḍʿah): A piece of flesh; used in the hadith to describe the penis as just a body part.
باطن الكف (bāṭin al-kaff): The inner part of the palm including the inner surfaces of the fingers.
الحائل (al-ḥā'il): Barrier; a covering that prevents direct skin contact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is the primary proof for the Hanafi position that touching the penis does not nullify wudu?
A) Hadith of Busrah bint Safwan
B) Hadith of Talq ibn Ali
C) Hadith of Abu Hurayrah
D) Hadith of Aisha

Key Takeaway
Touching the penis does not nullify wudu because it is merely a piece of flesh, as confirmed by the hadith of Talq and the practice of most Companions.

Ruling on Touching the Penis: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on wudu nullification by touch

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the penis and evaluate the strength of the opposing hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Touching the penis does not nullify wudu – the hadith of Talq rules by principle, not by specific command.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on whether touching the penis invalidates wudu. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Talq ibn Ali, which reasons that the penis is merely a piece of one's own flesh, while the Shafi'i school cites the hadith of Busra bint Safwan commanding wudu. The commentary engages in detailed hadith criticism to prefer the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: touching the penis does not nullify wudu. The act itself is permissible, but washing the hand is recommended.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
The Shafi'i school holds that touching the penis nullifies wudu, based on the hadith of Busra: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi response involves hadith criticism: the hadith of Talq is stronger (men narrators, more reliable), while Busra's hadith is weak (many scholars, including Yahya ibn Ma'in, declared it unsound). Also, Talq's hadith is based on a rational principle (ta'lil) that cannot be abrogated.
focus on the ta'lil argument
4
Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis do not need to renew wudu after touching; Shafi'is must renew wudu before prayer. This affects the validity of prayers in daily life.
5
Note the istihbab ruling
Even though touching does not nullify wudu, it is recommended (mustahabb) to wash the hand, as stated in al-Mabsut.
This reconciles the hadith of Busra by interpreting 'wudu' as hand-washing.

عنهم سخرنا منه. ومما يدل على انقطاع حديث بسرة باطناً أن أمر النواقض مما يحتاج الخاص والعام إليه وقد ثبت عن علي وعمار بن ياسر وعبد الله بن مسعود وعبد الله وحذيفة بن اليمان وعمران بن الحصين وأبي الدرداء وسعد بن أبي وقاص أنهم لا يرون النقض وإن روى عن غيرهم خلافه . وفي السنن للدراقطني حدثنا محمد بن الحسن النقاش أخبرنا . عبد الله بن يحيى القاضي السرخسي أخبرنا رجاء بن مرجا الحافظ قال: اجتمعنا في مسجد الخيف أنا وأحمد بن حنبل وعلي بن المديني ويحيى بن معين فتناظرنا في مس الذكر فقال يحيى بن معين : يتوضأ منه وقال علي بن المديني بقول الكوفيين وتقلد قولهم. واحتج يحيى بن معين بحديث بسرة بنت صفوان واحتج علي بن المديني بحديث قيس بن طلق وقال ليحيى : كيف تتقلد إسناد بسرة ومروان أرسل شرطياً حتى رد جوابها إليه؟ وقال يحيى : وقد أكثر الناس في قيس بن طلق ولا يحتج بحديثه فقال ابن حنبل : كلا الأمرين على ما قلتما. فقال يحيى : حدثنا مالك عن نافع عن ابن عمر أنه توضأ من مس الذكر فقال ابن المديني : كان ابن مسعود يقول : لا يتوضأ منه وإنما هو بضعة من جسدك. فقال يحيى عمن قال عن سفيان عن أبي قيس عن هذيل عن عبد الله، وإذا اجتمع ابن مسعود وابن عمر فابن مسعود أولى أن يتبع. فقال ابن حنبل : نعم ولكن أبو قيس لا يحتج بحديثه. فقال : حدثني أبو نعيم أخبرنا مسعر عن عمير بن سعيد عن عمار بن ياسر قال : ما أبالي مسسته أو أنفي فقال ابن حنبل : عمار وابن عمر استويا فمن شاء أخذ بهذا ومن شاء أخذ بهذا. ثم قال الحافظ: وإن سلكنا طريق الجمع جعل مس الذكر كناية عما يخرج منه وهو من أسرار البلاغة يسكتون عن ذكر الشيء ويرمزون عليه بذكر ما هو من روادفه، فلما كان مس الذكر غالباً يرادف خروج الحدث منه ويلازمه عبر به عنه كما عبر الله تعالى بالمجيء من الغائط عما يقصد لأجله ويحل فيه فيتطابق طريقا الكتاب والسنة في التعبير فيصار إلى هذا الدفع التعارض والله الموفق للصواب. ويستحب لمن مس ذكره أن يغسل يده، صرح به صاحب المبسوط وهذا أحد ما حمل به حدیث بسرة فقال : أو المراد بالوضوء غسل اليد استحباباً كما في قوله «الوضوء قبل الطعام ينفي الفقر وبعده ينفي اللمم لكن في البدائع ما يفيد تقييد الاستحباب بما إذا كان الاستنجاء بالأحجار دون الماء وهو حسن كما لا يخفى .
هـ.
وإن
للحافظ ابن حجر قال بعد أن ذكر حديث بسرة ورواه الترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه من طريق هشام بن عروة عن أبيه عن مروان به قال الترمذي : حسن صحيح اهـ فليتأمل. قوله : (وإن روى عن غيرهم خلافه) لا ينافي ذلك ما قدمه عن شرح الآثار لأن روايته عنهم لا تقتضي افتاءهم به ولا أنهم يروونه فافهم.
قوله : (لكن في البدائع ما يفيد الاستحباب الخ قال في النهر : ما في البدائع إنما هو فيما إذا
From Mulazim ibn Amr from Abdullah ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali from his father from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he was asked about a man who touches his penis during prayer, and he said: 'Is it but a piece of your flesh?' And Ibn Hibban narrated it in his Sahih. Al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is the best thing narrated on this topic and the most authentic. Al-Tahawi also narrated it and said: This is a sound hadith, not confused in its chain or text. So this is a sound hadith that opposes the hadith of Busra bint Safwan. And the hadith of Talq is preferred over the hadith of Busra because the hadith of men is stronger since they are more preservers of knowledge and more precise; therefore, the testimony of two women is made equivalent to the testimony of one man. Al-Tahawi narrated from Ibn al-Madini that he said: The hadith of Mulazim ibn Amr is better than the hadith of Busra. And from Amr ibn Ali al-Fallas that he said: The hadith of Talq is more firmly established with us than the hadith of Busra bint Safwan. And the statement of al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that the hadith of Talq is agreed to be weak is not hidden from you what is in it, since you have known what al-Tirmidhi and others said that the hadith of Busra was weakened by a group, to the extent that Yahya ibn Ma'in said: Three hadiths are not authentic from the Messenger of Allah, among them the hadith of touching the penis. And also the statement of al-Nawawi in preferring the hadith of Busra that the hadith of Talq is abrogated because his coming to the Prophet was in the first year of Hijra while the Prophet was building his mosque, and the narrator of the hadith of Busra is Abu Huraira, and Abu Huraira only came to the Prophet in the seventh year of Hijra, so it is not necessary because the appearance of Talq at that time and his return does not negate his later return; they narrated from him a weak hadith: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' And they said: He heard from the Prophet the abrogating and abrogated. Also because the hadith of Talq is not subject to abrogation because it was issued by way of reasoning, for he, peace be upon him, mentioned that the penis is a piece of flesh, so its touching has no effect on nullification, and this meaning does not accept abrogation, as in Miraj al-Diraya. And also the statement of al-Nawawi that the hadith of Talq is interpreted as touching over a barrier because he said: I asked him about touching the penis during prayer, and apparent is that a person does not touch his penis in prayer without a barrier, is refuted because his reasoning with his saying 'Is it but a piece of your flesh?' precludes such interpretation. And 'bada'a' with fath of the single letter is a piece of flesh. And in Sharh al-Athar of al-Tahawi: We do not know any companion who gave a fatwa for wudu from touching the penis except Ibn Umar, and most of them opposed him in that. And he narrated from Ibn Uyayna that he counted a group who did not know the hadith, meaning the hadith of Busra, and whoever we saw narrating it, he had a slight bias. He said: And other than the palm of the hand is excluded, such as the tips of the fingers and between them, and the edge of the fingers and the edge of the palm. And the ruling is specific to the inside of the palm, which is the palm with the insides of the fingers, because pleasure is only by that, end. His statement: (Indeed you have known what al-Tirmidhi said etc.) I say: That is not known from what preceded, but rather what is in Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah from Ibn Abbas ... and we mocked them. And among the evidence for the breaking of the chain of Busra's hadith internally is that the matter of nullifiers is something that both the elite and common need, and it is established from Ali, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Abdullah, Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, Imran ibn Husayn, Abu al-Darda', and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that they do not consider nullification, even if contrary is reported from others. In Sunan al-Daraqutni: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Naqqash narrated to us, Abdullah ibn Yahya al-Qadi al-Sarakhsi informed us, Raja' ibn Marja al-Hafiz informed us, he said: We gathered in Masjid al-Khayf, I and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ali ibn al-Madini, and Yahya ibn Ma'in, and we debated about touching the penis. Yahya ibn Ma'in said: He performs wudu from it. Ali ibn al-Madini said according to the Kufans and adhered to their view. Yahya ibn Ma'in argued with the hadith of Busra, and Ali ibn al-Madini argued with the hadith of Qays ibn Talq. He said to Yahya: How can you rely on the chain of Busra when Marwan sent a policeman until he returned her answer to him? Yahya said: People have said much about Qays ibn Talq, and his hadith is not used as evidence. Ibn Hanbal said: Both matters are as you said. Yahya said: Malik narrated to us from Nafi' from Ibn Umar that he performed wudu from touching the penis. Ibn al-Madini said: Ibn Mas'ud used to say: He does not perform wudu from it, it is but a piece of your body. Yahya said in response from Sufyan from Abu Qays from Hudhayl from Abdullah; and if Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar are together, Ibn Mas'ud is more worthy to be followed. Ibn Hanbal said: Yes, but Abu Qays's hadith is not used as evidence. He said: Abu Nu'aym narrated to us, Mas'ir narrated from Umayr ibn Sa'id from Ammar ibn Yasir, who said: I don't care whether I touch it or my nose. Ibn Hanbal said: Ammar and Ibn Umar are equal; whoever wishes takes this, whoever wishes takes that. Then the hafiz said: And if we take the path of reconciliation, we make touching the penis a metonymy for what comes out of it, which is among the secrets of eloquence; they remain silent about mentioning the thing and allude to it by mentioning what is among its concomitants. Since touching the penis for the most part is concomitant with the emission of the event from it and accompanies it, it is expressed by it just as Allah expressed by coming from the toilet for what is intended for it and occurs in it, so the way of the Book and Sunnah agree in expression, so we adopt this to repel the contradiction. And Allah is the guide to correctness. And it is recommended for whoever touches his penis to wash his hand, as stated by the author of al-Mabsut, and this is one of the interpretations of the hadith of Busra. He said: Or by wudu is meant washing the hand as a recommendation, as in the hadith: 'Wudu before food removes poverty and after it removes insanity' but in al-Bada'i there is something that restricts the recommendation to when the istinja is with stones without water, and that is good, as is not hidden. His statement: (Even if contrary is reported from others) does not contradict what he previously presented from Sharh al-Athar, because their narration from them does not necessitate their giving fatwa with it or that they narrated it, so understand. His statement: (But in al-Bada'i there is something that indicates the recommendation...) al-Nahr said: What is in al-Bada'i is only when
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on whether touching the penis nullifies wudu. The author presents the Hanafi position that it does not, supporting it with the hadith of Talq ibn Ali (marfu'): 'Is it but a piece of your flesh?' The Shafi'i position relies on the hadith of Busra bint Safwan that commands wudu. The commentary engages in extensive hadith criticism: it argues that Talq's hadith is stronger in transmission (since narrators are men, who are more precise) and that Busra's hadith is weak, with many scholars like Yahya ibn Ma'in declaring it unsound. It also refutes the claim that Talq's hadith is abrogated, arguing that it is based on a rational principle (ta'lil) that cannot be abrogated. The passage further discusses that if one touches the penis, it is recommended (mustahabb) to wash the hand, as stated in al-Mabsut, and this is one interpretation of Busra's hadith—that 'wudu' there means washing the hand, not the full ablution. The author also cites a gathering of hadith scholars (Ahmad, Ibn al-Madini, Yahya ibn Ma'in) where the dispute is debated, with Ibn Hanbal suggesting both views are possible but preferring the Kufan (Hanafi) view. The passage concludes with a suggestion to reconcile by interpreting 'touching the penis' as a metonymy for emission of ceremonial impurity, aligning with Quranic expression. The overall thrust is to establish the Hanafi ruling as the correct one.

Key Terms
بضعة (bada'a): A piece of flesh; used in the hadith to describe the penis as just a part of the body.
الوضوء (al-wudu): Ritual washing of specific body parts before prayer.
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the male genitals; the legal issue is whether it is a nullifier of wudu.
النقض (al-naqd): Nullification; breaking of wudu.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an act that is rewardable but not obligatory, not sinful to leave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person touches his penis with his palm?
A) Wudu is nullified and must be renewed before prayer.
B) Wudu remains valid; it is recommended to wash the hand.
C) Wudu is nullified only if done intentionally.
D) Wudu is nullified and the person must perform ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Touching the penis does not nullify wudu in the Hanafi school; the evidence is the hadith of Talq with a rational principle that does not accept abrogation.

Touching the Private Part: Does It Break Wudu?
Discusses the Hanafi stance on touching the private part and rebuts the opposing proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the private part and explain the Hanafi response to the opposing evidence.

Core Idea
Touching the private part does not break wudu—Companion practice and metaphorical interpretation override the literal hadith.

The issue of whether touching one's own private part invalidates wudu is a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school holds that it does not, based on the practice of many Companions and a careful interpretation of the relevant hadith. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: touching the private part does not break wudu. Note that it is permissible and washing the hand is recommended.
2
Identify the opposing evidence
Recognize the hadith of Basra bint Safwan as the primary proof for those who say wudu is broken.
The hadith is: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith is either metaphorical for emission or means hand-washing, not full wudu. The practice of the Companions (e.g., Ali, Ibn Mas'ud) overrides a literal reading.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the established practice of the Companions.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the ruling: a Hanafi may touch his private part without needing to renew wudu. The difference with the Shafi'i school affects daily worship.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether touching one's own private part breaks wudu. The Hanafi position is that it does not, supported by the practice of many Companions such as Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ammar. The author presents a debate among early scholars including Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Yahya ibn Ma'in, and Ali ibn al-Madini, where the latter argued for the Kufan (Hanafi) view. The hadith of Basra (that touching the penis requires wudu) is reconciled by interpreting it as a metaphor for the emission of discharge or by understanding 'wudu' to mean washing the hand only. The recommendation to wash the hand is mentioned, with a note from al-Bada'i' that this applies when istinja was done with stones. The author affirms that the Hanafi view is correct and the conflict between the hadith and the Companions' practice is resolved through interpretation.

Key Terms
مس الذكر (mas al-dhakar): Touching one's own penis with the hand.
الوضوء (al-wudu): The ritual ablution before prayer; in this context, it sometimes refers to simply washing the hands.
بسرة بنت صفوان (Basra bint Safwan): A female Companion from whom a hadith is narrated that touching the penis requires wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It does not break wudu, and no action is required.
C) It breaks wudu, but only washing the hand is sufficient.
D) It does not break wudu, but it is recommended to wash the hand.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, touching the private part does not break wudu, supported by Companion practice and a metaphorical interpretation of the hadith.

Does Touching a Woman Break Wudu? The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Explains the Hanafi position and refutes the Shafi'i view with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on touching a woman and wudu, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using Quranic exegesis and usul principles.

Core Idea
Touching a woman does not break wudu because 'lams' in the Quran means sexual intercourse, not mere contact.

This lesson examines a classic fiqh dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over whether touching a woman invalidates wudu. The issue hinges on the interpretation of the Quranic verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' (or you have touched women). We will analyze the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i evidence, and the three Hanafi responses as presented in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: touching a woman (without desire or emission) does not break wudu. This is the mufta bihi position from the zahir al-riwayah.
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on this.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the Shafi'i position: touching a woman breaks the toucher's wudu absolutely, with some exceptions for the touched party.
Imam al-Shafi'i bases this on the literal meaning of 'lams'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the Quranic verse and linguistic usage of 'lams' for touch.
The verse 'or you have touched women' (4:43) and the linguistic definition support the Shafi'i view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Work through the three Hanafi arguments: (1) usul-based rejection of dual meaning, (2) lexical shift when 'lams' is connected to women, (3) contextual preference for intercourse based on the verse structure.
These responses show the depth of Hanafi istinbat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: a Hanafi does not need to renew wudu after touch; a Shafi'i does. This affects daily practice, especially for imams.
Some Hanafi scholars advised caution for imams due to the respected difference.

ذات رحم محرم أو صغيره لا تشتهي فإنه لا ينقض على الأصح بخلاف العجوز فالصحيح النقض، وهذه المسألة قد وقع الاختلاف فيها في الصدر الأول وهو اختلاف معتبر حتى قال بعض مشايخنا: ينبغي لمن يؤم أن يحتاط فيه، فمذهب عمرو بن مسعود وعبد الله بن عمر وجماعة من التابعين كمذهب الشافعي، ومذهب علي وابن عباس وجماعة من التابعين كمذهبنا استدل الشافعي بقوله تعالى أو لامستم النساء [النساء: 43] فإن اللمس يطلق على الجس باليد قال تعالى فلمسوه بأيديهم [الأنعام: 7] وبقول أهل اللغة اللمس يكون باليد وبغيرها وقد يكون بالجماع فنعمل بمقتضى اللمس مطلقاً، فمتى التقت البشرتان انتقض سواء كان بيد أو جماع. ولأئمتنا في الجواب عن هذا أوجه أحدهما ما ذكره الأصوليون كفخر الإسلام البزدوي أن حقيقة اللمس يكون باليد وأن الجماع مجاز فيه لكن المجاز مراد الإجماع حتى حل للجنب التيمم بالآية فبطلت الحقيقة لأنه يستحيل اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد ثانيهما وهو المذكور في بعض كتب الفقه أن اللمس إذا قرن بالمرأة كان حقيقة في الجماع يؤيده أن الملامسة مفاعلة من اللمس وذلك يكون بين اثنين فصاعداً، وعندهم لا يشترط اللمس من الطرفين. ثالثها أن اللمس مشترك بين اللمس باليد وبين الجماع ورجحنا الحمل على الجماع بالمعنى وذلك أنه سبحانه وتعالى أفاض في بيان حكم الحدثين الأصغر والأكبر عند القدرة على الماء بقوله إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة إلى قوله وإن كنتم جنباً فأطهروا [النساء: 43] فبين أنه الغسل، ثم شرع في بيان الحال عند عدم القدرة عليه بقوله وإن كنتم مرضى أو على سفر إلى قوله فتيمموا صعيداً [النساء: 43] الخ. فإذا حملت الآية على الجماع كان بياناً لحكم الحدثين بين حكمهما عند وجوده فيتم الغرض لأن بالناس حاجة الأصغر والأكبر عند عدم الماء كما استنجى بالأحجار دون الماء وتلوثت يده لا مطلقاً وذلك أنه قال: إن الحديث أعني قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من مس ذكره فليتوضأ محمول على غسل اليدين لأن الصحابة رضي الله تعالى عنهم كانوا يستنجون بالأحجار دون الماء فإذا مسوه بأيديهم كانت تتلوث خصوصاً في أيام الصيف، فأمروا بالغسل اهـ. ولا يخفى أن إطلاق السرخسي أولى عملاً بعموم من اهـ ويؤيد هذا أن الغسل عند التلوّث قد يكون واجباً فيكون أمراً بإزالة النجاسة وهو واجب لا مستحب، فالأولى حمله على غسل اليد مطلقاً كما قاله السرخسي. ومما يدل على ما ذكره من حمل حديث بسرة على ذلك ما ذكره الحافظ ابن حجر في تخريج أحاديث الهداية وعن مصعب بن سعيد قال: مسست ذكري ومعي المصحف فقال لي أبي توضأ ثم اخرج في طريقه قال: فقال لي أبي قم فاغسل يدك. اهـ. ولعل حكمة الأمر بالغسل كون ذلك محل خروج النجاسة فربما تكون في اليد أو المحل رطوبة سيما عند الاستنجاء وذلك مظنة
His saying: (and a woman, in the genitive as a conjunction to 'dhakar') meaning: touching the skin of a woman does not break wudu at all, whether with desire or not. Al-Shafi'i said: the wudu of the toucher is broken absolutely, whether with desire and intention or not. He has two opinions regarding the one touched, the more correct being that it breaks wudu unless she is a mahram relative or a young child not desired, in which case it does not break according to the soundest view, contrary to an old woman where the correct view is that it breaks. This issue was disputed in the first generation, a significant disagreement such that some of our shaykhs said: one should be cautious in it. The school of Amr ibn Mas'ud, Abdullah ibn Umar, and a group of tabi'un is like al-Shafi'i, and the school of Ali and Ibn Abbas and a group of tabi'un is like our school. Al-Shafi'i used as evidence the verse 'or you have touched women' (4:43), for 'lams' is applied to touching with the hand, and the verse 'they touched it with their hands' (6:7), and the statement of linguists that 'lams' occurs with the hand and other things and may mean intercourse. So we act on the general implication of 'lams'. Whenever two skins meet, wudu is broken, whether by hand or intercourse. Our imams have several responses: one is what the usul scholars like Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi mentioned, that the real meaning of 'lams' is with the hand and intercourse is metaphorical, but the metaphor is intended by consensus such that the junub is allowed tayammum by the verse, so the real meaning is invalidated because it is impossible for both to be intended by one word. The second is from some fiqh books: 'lams' when connected to women is real for intercourse, supported by the fact that mulamasah is a mutual form requiring two parties, and they do not require mutual touching. The third is that 'lams' is shared between touch by hand and intercourse, and we prefer the meaning of intercourse because Allah explained the rules of minor and major hadath when water is available, and then explained the case when water is absent. If the verse is interpreted as intercourse, it clarifies the ruling for both hadath at the time of presence, and the purpose is fulfilled. As for the hadith 'whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu', it is interpreted as washing the hands because the Companions used stones for istinja and their hands would become soiled, especially in summer, so they were commanded to wash. The absolute view of al-Sarakhsi is preferable, and this is supported by the fact that washing due to filth may be obligatory, so it is an order to remove impurity, which is obligatory not recommended. Therefore, the preferred interpretation is to wash the hand absolutely, as al-Sarakhsi said. Evidence for this interpretation of the hadith of Basra is what al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar mentioned in his Takhrij...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether touching a woman breaks wudu. The Hanafi school holds that it does not, whether with desire or not, while al-Shafi'i holds that it does for the toucher (with some exceptions for the touched). The author presents the Shafi'i evidence from the Quranic verse 'or you have touched women' and the linguistic definition of 'lams'. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) 'lams' in the verse means intercourse, not just touching, because the real meaning is impossible when applied to tayammum for the junub; (2) when 'lams' is connected to women, it becomes a real term for intercourse; (3) it is a shared term, but we prefer the meaning of intercourse because the context of the verse discusses both hadath and water availability. The passage also discusses the hadith of Basra regarding touching the penis and interprets it as washing the hand due to dirt, not full wudu. The author concludes that the absolute view of al-Sarakhsi (washing hands) is preferable.

Key Terms
مس المرأة (mas al-mar'ah): Touching the skin of a woman with the hand.
اللمس (al-lams): Linguistically, it can mean touch by hand or sexual intercourse. In the Quranic context, the Hanafi school takes it as intercourse.
الملامسة (al-mulamasah): A mutual form of lams, implying contact between two parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does 'lams' in the Quranic verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' mean?
A) Any touching of women by hand.
B) Sexual intercourse with women.
C) Both touching and intercourse.
D) Touching with desire only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets 'lams' in the wudu verse as sexual intercourse, not mere touch, which is supported by three arguments: lexical, contextual, and usul-based.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Obligatory Acts of Ghusl: The Hanafi Ruling on Madmadah and Istinshaq
Ruling with proof: establishing the obligatory status of madmadah and istinshaq in ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory acts (fard) of ghusl according to the Hanafi school, and explain why madmadah and istinshaq are included, using the Quran and Hadith as proof.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are fard in ghusl because the Quran commands complete purification, and the mouth and nose are part of the body without hardship.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the obligatory acts of ghusl (ritual bath). While some schools consider rinsing the mouth and sniffing water into the nose to be recommended (sunnah), the Hanafi school holds them to be obligatory (fard). This lesson will guide you through the primary evidence from the Quran and Hadith, and the Hanafi response to the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic fard of ghusl
According to the text, washing the mouth, nose, and entire body is obligatory. This is the ruling stated in Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
The base text uses 'fard' to mean the obligatory act.
2
Understand the Quranic command
Quran 4:43 commands complete purification. The Hanafi principle: the imperative indicates obligation. Areas of extreme hardship (like eyes) are excluded, but mouth and nose are not.
The verse is 'wa in kuntum junuban fa’t’ahharu'.
3
Examine the Hadith evidence
The hadith 'Under every hair is janabah, so wet the hair and clean the skin' implies thorough washing. Additionally, a specific hadith states: 'They are two fards in janabah and two sunnahs in wudu'.
This explicit hadith directly supports obligation in ghusl.
4
Respond to the fitrah objection
The opposing school uses the fitrah hadith (listing madmadah and istinshaq among ten acts of fitrah) to argue sunnah status. The Hanafi response: fitrah means religion, which includes obligatory acts; the explicit hadith overrides the general fitrah list.
The Prophet said 'Every child is born upon the fitrah', meaning Islam.

كتاب الطهارة
قوله: (وفرض الغسل غسل فمه وأنفه وبدنه قد تقديم وجه تقدم الوضوء على الغسل. والواو في قوله وفرض إما للاستئناف أو للعطف على قوله «فرض الوضوء». والفرض مصدر بمعنى المفروض لأن المصدر يذكر ويراد به الزمان والمكان والفاعل والمفعول في الكشاف. وقوله «الغسل يعني غسل الجنابة والحيض والنفاس كذا في السراج الوهاج، وظاهره أن المضمضة والاستنشاق ليستا شرطين في الغسل المسنون حتى يصح بدونهما . ثم اعلم أن الكلام في الغسل في مواضع في تفسيره لغة وشرعاً وفي سببه وركنه وشرائطه وسننه وآدابه وصفته وحكمه. أما تفسيره لغة فهو بالضم اسم من الاغتسال وهو تمام غسل الجسد واسم للماء الذي يغتسل به أيضاً، ومنه في حديث ميمونة فوضعت له غسلاً كذا في المغرب. وقال النووي: إنه بفتح الغين وضمها لغتان والفتح أفصح وأشهر عند أهل اللغة والضم هو الذي تستعمله الفقهاء أو أكثرهم واصطلاحاً هو المعنى الأول اللغوي وهو غسل البدن وقد تقدم تفسير الغسل بالفتح لغة وشرعاً. وأما ركنه فهو إسالة الماء على جميع ما يمكن إسالته عليه من البدن من غير حرج مرة واحدة حتى لو بقيت لمعة لم يصبها الماء لم يجز الغسل وإن كانت يسيرة لقوله تعالى وإن كنتم جنباً فاطهروا [النساء : ٤٣] أمر الله سبحانه وتعالى بالأطهر بضم الهاء لأن أصله تطهر فادغمت التاء في الطاء لقرب المخرج فجيء بحرف الوصل ليتوصل بها إلى النطق فصار اطهروا وبعض من لا خبرة له ولا دراية يقرأ بالأطهار وما ذاك إلا لحرمانه من العربية كذا في غاية البيان. وهو تطهير جميع البدن واسم البدن يقع على الظاهر والباطن إلا أن ما يتعذر إيصال الماء إليه خارج عن قضية النص، وكذا ما يتعسر لأن المتعسر منفي كالمتعذر كداخل العينين فإن في غسلهما من الحرج ما لا يخفى فإن العين شحم لا تقبل الماء، وقد كف تكلف له بصر من كابن عمر وابن عباس ولهذا لا تغسل العين إذا اكتحل بكحل نجس، ولهذا وجبت المضمضة والاستنشاق في الغسل لأنه لا حرج في غسلهما فشملهما نص الكتاب من غير معارض كما شملهما قوله لا تحت كل شعرة جنابة فبلوا الشعر وانقوا البشرة (1) رواه الترمذي من غير معارض. والبشرة ظاهر الجلد بخلافهما في الوضوء لأن الواجب فيه غسل الوجه ولا تقع المواجهة بداخلهما ، وأما قوله له عشر من الفطرة وذكر منها المضمضة والاستنشاق (2) لا يعارضه إذ كونهما من الفطرة لا ينفي الوجوب لأنها الدين وهو أعم منه قال صلى الله عليه وسلم «كل مولود يولد على الفطرة» (3) والمراد أعلى الواجبات على ما هو أعلى الأقوال، وهو على هذا فلا حاجة إلى حمل المروي على حالة الحدث بدليل قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إنهما فرضان في الجناية سنتان في الوضوء» ما عن أبي هريرة أنه جعل المضمضة والاستنشاق للجنب ثلاثاً فريضة لكن يعني كأنه انعقد الإجماع على خروج اثنين منها وهو ضعيف، كذا في فتح القدير. والمراد بأعلى الواجبات الإسلام لكن قال أبو نصر الدبوسي كما نقله عنه الحاوي الحصري : لا يصح أن يعنى ما مصدراً طهر من باب التفعيل أصله تطهر قلبت التاء طاء ثم أدغمت ثم جيء بهمزة الوصل للنطق بالساكن قوله : (واسم) البدن يقع على الظاهر والباطن الخ) نقل الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي عن المغرب وغيره أن البدن من المنكب إلى الألية قال : وحينئذ فالرأس والعنق واليد والرجل خارجة لغة داخلة تبعاً شرعاً .اهـ. قوله : (من غير معارض متعلق بقوله شملهما الثاني. قوله : (كأنه : عن أبي هريرة الخ) الظاهر أن فاعل يعني ضمير يعود إلى الحامل المفهوم من المصدر في قوله «فلا حاجة إلى حمل المروي والمعنى كأن الحامل قصد بالحديث الذي استدل به ما روي عن أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه تأمل قوله
